Additional information: Chief Complaint from Nursing Triage Note : Chief Complaint
12/5/2022 20:40 EST Chief Complaint Chief Complaint .
 
History of Present Illness
The patient presents following motor vehicle collision. The onset was 7 hours ago. The Collision was rear impact and low speed. The patient was
the driver. There were safety mechanisms including seat belt. lower back, neck, felt like he went forward and hit the seat abruptly . The degree of pain
is minimal. The degree of bleeding is none. Risk factors consist of none. Therapy today: none. Associated symptoms: back pain, denies chest pain,
denies loss of consciousness, denies altered level of consciousness, denies dizziness and denies syncope. Additional history: happened 4 hr prior to
arrival, ambulatory on scene.
 
Review of Systems
Constitutional symptoms: No fever, no chills.
Skin symptoms: No rash,

Endocrine symptoms: No polyuria,
Hematologic/Lymphatic symptoms: Bleeding tendency negative, bruising tendency negative.
Allergy/immunologic symptoms: No food allergies,
Additional review of systems information: All other systems reviewed and otherwise negative.

Patient: KIPER, JAMES R MRN: V000416364 FIN: V[PHONE-428]
Age: 46 years Sex: Male DOB: 4/29/1976
Associated Diagnoses: None
Author: BELL, STEPHEN, PA-EMR
 
HPI:
 
46-year-old male presents to triage as a restrained ever involved in a 2 vehicle collision earlier today. Patient was at a low
stop sign when he was rear-ended by another vehicle going about 5 mph he got out of his vehicle and went to get some
information and insurance, and then the guy stuck around for about 3 or 4 minutes and they took off in his vehicle than 2
blocks later that person got into the other accident that occurred 1 more time as well. He complains of neck and low back
pain. No airbag deployment. No compartment intrusion. Did not hit his head on anything in the vehicle. No loss
consciousness. No vision changes or vomiting. Complains of mild headache as well. Rates his pain a 4 out of 10.
 
History review:
 
Past medical, surgical and social history reviewed in the nursing notes. I agree with these notes.

As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be
given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common
side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may
include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and
driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or
questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time,
which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal
symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and
nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Education Materials
Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult
After a motor vehicle collision, it is common to have injuries to the head, face, arms, and body. These injuries may include:
Page 28 of 93

MEH Mary & Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: KIPER, JAMES RAY DOB/Age/Sex: 4/29/1976 47 years Male
MRN: V000416364 Account #: V[PHONE-390]
LEGEND: *=Corrected, @=Abnormal, C=Critical, L=Low, H=High, f=Footnote, #=Interpretive Data, R=Ref Lab
Report Request ID: 207545257 4/24/2024 09:00 EDT
Emergency
• Cuts.
• Burns.
• Bruises.
• Sore muscles and muscle strains.
• Headaches.
You may have stiffness and soreness for the first several hours. You may feel worse after waking up the first morning after the collision.
These injuries often feel worse for the first 24–48 hours. Your injuries should then begin to improve with each day. How quickly you
improve often depends on:
• The severity of the collision.
• The number of injuries you have.
• The location and nature of the injuries.
• Whether you were wearing a seat belt and whether your airbag deployed.
A head injury may result in a concussion, which is a type of brain injury that can have serious effects. If you have a concussion, you
should rest as told by your health care provider. You must be very careful to avoid having a second concussion.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider.
• If you were prescribed antibiotic medicine, take or apply it as told by your health care provider. Do not stop using the antibiotic
even if your condition improves.
If you have a wound or a burn:
• Clean your wound or burn as told by your health care provider.
—46 Wash it with mild soap and water.
—46 Rinse it with water to remove all soap.
—46 Pat it dry with a clean towel. Do not rub it.
—46 If you were told to put an ointment or cream on the wound, do so as told by your health care provider.
• Follow instructions from your health care provider about how to take care of your wound or burn. Make sure you:
—46 Know when and how to change or remove your bandage (dressing). Always wash your hands with soap and water
before and after you change your dressing. If soap and water are not available, use hand sanitizer.

Emergency
—46 Leave stitches (sutures), skin glue, or adhesive strips in place, if this applies. These skin closures may need to stay
in place for 2 weeks or longer. If adhesive strip edges start to loosen and curl up, you may trim the loose edges. Do not
remove adhesive strips completely unless your health care provider tells you to do that.
• Do not:
—46 Scratch or pick at the wound or burn.
—46 Break any blisters you may have.
—46 Peel any skin.
• Avoid exposing your burn or wound to the sun.
• Raise (elevate) the wound or burn above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down. This will help reduce pain,
pressure, and swelling. If you have a wound or burn on your face, you may want to sleep with your head elevated. You may do
this by putting an extra pillow under your head.
• Check your wound or burn every day for signs of infection. Check for:
—46 More redness, swelling, or pain.
—46 More fluid or blood.
—46 Warmth.
—46 Pus or a bad smell.
Activity
• Rest. Rest helps your body to heal. Make sure you:
—46 Get plenty of sleep at night. Avoid staying up late.
—46 Keep the same bedtime hours on weekends and weekdays.
• Ask your health care provider if you have any lifting restrictions. Lifting can make neck or back pain worse.
• Ask your health care provider when you can drive, ride a bicycle, or use heavy machinery. Your ability to react may be slower if
you injured your head. Do not do these activities if you are dizzy.
• If you are told to wear a brace on an injured arm, leg, or other part of your body, follow instructions from your health care
provider about any activity restrictions related to driving, bathing, exercising, or working.
General instructions
• If directed, put ice on the injured areas. This can help with pain and swelling.
—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day.

• You have a fever.

—46 Dizziness or balance problems.

—46 Increased sensitivity to noise or light.

—46 Anxiety or irritability.
—46 Memory problems.
—46 Trouble concentrating or paying attention.
—46 Sleep problems.
—46 Feeling tired all the time.
Get help right away if:
• You have:
—46 Numbness, tingling, or weakness in your arms or legs.
—46 Severe neck pain, especially tenderness in the middle of the back of your neck.
—46 Changes in bowel or bladder control.
—46 Increasing pain in any area of your body.
—46 Swelling in any area of your body, especially your legs.
—46 Shortness of breath or light-headedness.
—46 Chest pain.
—46 Blood in your urine, stool, or vomit.
—46 Severe pain in your abdomen or your back.
—46 Severe or worsening headaches.
—46 Sudden vision loss or double vision.
• Your eye suddenly becomes red.
• Your pupil is an odd shape or size.
Summary
• After a motor vehicle collision, it is common to have injuries to the head, face, arms, and body.
• Follow instructions from your health care provider about how to take care of a wound or burn.

Every Minute Counts

and obesity Smoking
Cigarette Smoking
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline: 988
The 988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline is a national network of local crisis centers that provides free and confidential emotional support to
people in suicidal crisis or emotional distress 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. 
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.
• Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
Page 32 of 93

MEH Mary & Elizabeth Hospital

Emergency
• 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
• Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:
Nausea
Feeling of
"fullness" in
chest
Jaw Pain
Pain that travels
down one or
both arms
Fatigue/being
tired Anxiety Back Pain
Chest pressure,
squeezing, or
discomfort
Shortness of
breath
Sweating, or a
cold sweat
Feeling of
impending
doom
There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
• Fainting/dizziness
• Weakness
• Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.
Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure

at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes

Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.
Why Hands-Only CPR?
• Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
• Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
• 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse

Save a life!
4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.
• Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
1
PREVENT
INFECTIONS
• Take good care of
chronic conditions.
• Talk to your doctor
about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
2
PRACTICE GOOD
HYGIENE
• Wash your hands
frequently.
• Keep cuts or open
sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.
3
KNOW THE
SYMPTOMS
• Confusion or
disorientation
• Shortness of breath
• High heart rate
• Fever, shivering, or
feeling very cold
• Extreme pain or
discomfort
• Clammy or sweaty
skin
4 ACT FAST
• Get medical care
IMMEDIATELY if
you suspect sepsis
or if you have an
infection that is not
getting better or is
getting worse.
To learn more about sepsis and how to prevent infections, visit www.cdc.gov/sepsis.

AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL
| understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and
semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. | hereby agree that the
difference in the cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if | request one
at any point during my stay.
| hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under
any applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my
Authorized Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that | may have under
such insurance policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to
pursue such claim, right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan,
including the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by
the provisions of the Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").
| also authorize UofL Health to act on my behalf to (1) obtain copies of my insurance policy or benefit plan
documents from my insurer(s) or other Plan Administrator; (2) pursue appeals of adverse benefits decisions,
claims for breaches of fiduciary duty under ERISA, external appeal review under Federal or State statute,
administrative hearings, or legal actions to obtain payment from any payor; (3) disclose my protected health
information to my insurer(s), its affiliates, any plan fiduciary, or independent review organization that may be
involved in the resolution of claims, in connection with filing or appealing any claim for benefits due; and (4)
receive any notices in connection with mybenefit claims or appeals concerning same.
If my admission to UofL Health is a result of a work-related injury, | hereby waive any privilege | may have with
UofL Health, or other healthcare provider, and | hereby authorize these providers to provide the worker's
compensation administrator any information related to my injury or to my past relevant medical history. In the
event there is a dispute about the compensability of my claim or worker's compensation benefits, and if my
employer is not specifically determined by a Court of the Department of Labor to be responsible for worker's
compensation medical expenses for the condition or injury that is the basis of my admission, | agree to be
personally responsible for all such expenses. | further agree that, if my worker’s compensation claim is settled
with my employer on a disputed basis without a specific finding that such is compensable as a worker's
compensation injury, | (or my attorney, if | am represented) will withhold sufficient funds from any settlement to
pay all amounts owed to UofL Health for treatment of the condition which is the basis for this admission, and |
hereby grant an assignment to UofL Health for payment of all such expenses under such circumstances.
PERSONAL EQUIPMENT AND VALUABLES
| understand that UofL Health does not accept responsibility and will not reimburse me for the loss of money,
jewelry, eyewear, hearing aids, dentures, clothing or other personal property or valuables | bring to UofL Health.
| take full responsibility for such items and agree to release UofL Health from any and all liability from damage,
loss or theft of such items unless, as applicable, the items are deposited at UofL Health safe for safekeeping. |
also understand that | must inform a nurse if | bring any electrical equipment to UofL Health (e.g., home insulin
pumps; BiPAP machine, CPAP machine) and adhere to UofL Health policies regarding its uSe. | assume full
responsibility for such electrical equipment and for any injury caused by the use of the electrical equipment
brought from home.
COMMUNICATIONS
By providing my cell, landline, or any other phone number(s), | expressly consent to receiving communications
from UofL Health, its staff, its contractors, collection agents, and others, at any numbers | provide or that are
later acquired for me. These parties may use this information to contact me by live agent, voice mail, text
message, using an auto dialer or other computer assisted technology, pre-recorded message(s), or by any
other form of electronic communication for any purpose including, but not limited to, appointment and follow-up
health care reminders, scheduling, my account(s), assignment of benefits, and/or financial responsibility. |
understand that depending on my phone plan | could be charged for these calls or text messages. | agree to
provide new number(s) if my number(s) change(s). Providing these numbers is not a condition of receiving
healthcare services.

General Consent on Admission
The term “UofL Health” means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
| give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, | consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT
| have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. | consent to and authorize such care
including but not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services")
performed bymy admitting and treating physicians.
1acknowledge that not all health care providers including physicians, nurse anesthetists, nurse practitioners,
therapists, residents and students, are employees or agents of Uofl Health. Such individuals are independent
contractors who bill separately for their Services. | also understand that UofL Health is not responsible for nor
does it assume any liability for the acts or omissions of any independent contractor(s). | acknowledge there may
be supervised participation of health care students (medical students, nursing students, interns, residents and
non-physician clinical students).
| understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or
results of this treatment and/or examination and | have the right to make decisions concerning my health care,
including the right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
| understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, | may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or
any airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic
purposes. | also understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as
an emergency worker, fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although | will be informed of the right to
consent to testing for HIV or other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be
performed on previously gathered bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing.
Information concerning the fact that a test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and
be disclosed by UofL Health only as permitted by law.
FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY
| agree that | obligate myself and/or the Patient to pay the account(s) of Uofl Health in accordance with the
established rates and payment policy of UofL Health. | also understand that patient/guarantor payments can be
applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or
other sources.
| understand that if my Insurer denies all or any part of UofL Health's charges for any reason, or if | have no
insurance, | will be personally and fully responsible for payment of UofL Health’s charges. | am aware that |
must notify the Business Office and submit the completed application form if | believe | may qualify for financial
assistance. I/My Designated Health Care Representative authorizes billing by and direct payment to UofL
Health or to the physicians providing Services at UofL Health. | understand they will bill my insurance directly
for their Services, at a rate not to exceed the UofL Health’s or physician’s regular charges. Insurance includes
but is not limited to, my medical health insurance policy/policies, including my employee health benefit plan,
accident, worker's compensation benefits, motor vehicle insurance, casualty insurance, and uninsured or
underinsured insurance

MY INFORMATION
WL
The Law: There is a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996
(“HIPAA”). This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients’ treatment, contact,
and financial information. Taken together, this information is called your “Health Information”, There are also
other federal and/or state laws that require UofL Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of
Health Information, including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health;
developmental disabilities; treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and
counseling; HIV/AIDS; sexual assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic
abuse of an adult with a disability; child abuse and neglect.
Authorization and Notice of Privacy Practices (“NPP”):If my permission is required by law, by signing this
form | agree that UofL Health may receive, use and disclose my Health Information as set forth in this Consent
and as set forth in UofL Health’s NPP. | understand that | can find more information about my rights to my
Health Information, and about how UofL Health uses my Health Information, in the NPP. | acknowledge that if |
requested a copy of the NPP that I have been given a copy. | further understand that the NPP is available on
UofL Health’s website at: www.uoflhealth.org.
| agree that my permission applies to all of my Health Information in UofL Health's possession, including but not
limited to my contact information, problem list, diagnostic test results, medication list, allergy list, immunizations,
medical history, surgeries, procedures, and other clinically relevant data.
| understand that UofL Health cannot control how others that receive my Health Information will protect or use
my information. | understand that others may not be required by law to protect my Health Information.
Purposes for which my Health Information may be shared: | understand that UofL Health may receive, use,
and disclose my Health Information for the purposes outlined in the NPP. In particular, UofL Health may use
and disclose my Health Information for the following purposes:
Data Sharing Program Purposes: | understand and agree that the use and disclosure of my health
information for certain aspects of treatment at UofL Health may be disclosed to other people involved with my
care outside UofL Health. If | desire to revoke my consent, even in an emergency situation, |must notify UofL
Health’s Health Information Management Department by phone: [PHONE-339], option 2. | understand and
agree that my request will be evaluated to determine ifit is reasonable and inthe best interest of my health care
to comply with my request. | will be notified in writing of as to whether UofL Health will be able to grant my
request. If my request is granted and | am are in need of emergency treatment, UofL Health may end the
restriction if the information is needed to provide my care. (See our Notice of Privacy Practices for more
information on these types of uses and disclosures for further information.)
Fundraising Activities: UoflL Health relies on fundraising to help support caring for all patients. | give my
permission to be contacted relating to fundraising opportunities. If | prefer not to be contacted about fundraising,
| must notify UofL Health by email to: [EMAIL-126] or by phone [PHONE-337]
Operational Purposes: | agree that the contact information | give to UofL Health, such as telephone numbers
and email addresses, may be used by UofL Health and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with
me for operational purposes including appointment reminders, follow up treatment reminders, flu shot
reminders, and patient surveys.

Magnetic Resonance Imaging
Accession Exam STATUS Exam Date/Time Ordering Provider
07-MR-23-0001166 MRI Pelvis WO W Auth (Verified) 4/21/2023 14:52 EDT KAVALUKAS,SANDRA,
MD-PRO
Reason For Exam
(MRI Pelvis WO W) Anal fistula;Anal fistula
Report
History: Concern for anal fistula.
TECHNIQUE:
Multiplanar, multisequence MR images of the pelvis were performed before and after 14 cc of IV gadolinium contrast.
COMPARISON: CT pelvis exam dated [DOB-226].
FINDINGS:
Bone marrow signal throughout the pelvis is within normal limits. No abnormal enhancement of the bone marrow. No
intrapelvic mass or adenopathy. No significant free fluid. Heterogeneity of the prostate. Urinary bladder unremarkable.
Suspect linear defect at the posterior anus at the midline. Linear sinus tract extending to the left of midline as well as the
right of midline from the defect to the skin surface at the gluteal cleft inferiorly. No sizable fluid collection. There is some
susceptibility artifact suggesting either soft tissue gas or findings related to prior intervention. Tiny bilateral scrotal
hydroceles are noted.
IMPRESSION: Anal fissure suspected at the posterior midline with linear sinus tract extending bilaterally to the skin
surface at the inferior gluteal cleft consistent with fistulas. No sizable drainable abscess.
Dictated by: Ronald Meade, MD Signed by Ronald Meade, MD on 4/21/2023 11:02 PM

General Consent on Admission
The term “UofL Health” means Uofl. Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
| give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, | consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT
| have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. | consent to and authorize such care
including but not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services")
performed by my admitting and treating physicians.
| acknowledge that not all health care providers including physicians, nurse anesthetists, nurse practitioners,
therapists, residents and students, are employees or agents of UofL Health. Such individuals are independent
contractors who bill separately for their Services. | also understand that UofL Health is not responsible for nor
does it assume any liability for the acts or omissions of any independent contractor(s). | acknowledge there may
be supervised participation of health care students (medical students, nursing students, interns, residents and
non-physician clinical students).
| understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or
results of this treatment and/or examination and | have the right to make decisions concerning my health care,
including the right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
| understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, | may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or
any airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic
purposes. | also understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as
an emergency worker, fire fighter or policé-officer)to my bodily fluids, although I will be informed of the right to
consent to testing for HIV or other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be
performed on previously gathered bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained-to compe! such testing.
Information concerning the fact that a test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and
be disclosed by UofL Health only as permitted by law.
FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY
| agree that | obligate myself and/or the Patient to pay the account(s) of UofL Health in accordance with the
established rates and payment policy of UofL Health. | also understand that patient/guarantor payments can be
applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or
other sources.
| understand that if my Insurer denies all or any part of UofL Health’s charges for any reason, or if | have no
insurance, | will be personally and fully responsible for payment of UofL Health’s charges. | am aware that |
must notify the Business Office and submit the completed application form if | believe | may qualify for financial
assistance. I/My Designated Health Care Representative authorizes billing by and direct payment to UofL
Health or to the physicians providing Services at UofL Health. | understand they will bill my insurance directly
for their Services, at a rate not to exceed the UofL Health’s or physician’s regular charges. Insurance includes
but is not limited to, my medical health insurance policy/policies, including my employee health benefit plan,
accident, worker's compensation benefits, motor vehicle insurance, casualty insurance, and uninsured or
underinsured insurance

AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL
! understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and
semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. | hereby agree that the
difference in the cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if | request one
at any point during my stay.
| hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under
any applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my
Authorized Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that | may have under
such insurance policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to
pursue such claim, right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan,
including the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by
the provisions of the Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").
| also authorize UofL Health to act on my behalf to (1) obtain copies of my insurance policy or benefit plan
documents from my insurer(s) or other Plan Administrator; (2) pursue appeals of adverse benefits decisions,
claims for breaches of fiduciary duty under ERISA, external appeal review under Federal or State statute,
administrative hearings, or legal actions to obtain payment from any payor; (3) disclose my protected health
information to my insurer(s), its affiliates, any plan fiduciary, or independent review organization that may be
involved in the resolution of claims, in connection with filing or appealing any claim for benefits due; and (4)
receive any notices in connection with my benefit claims or appeals concerning same.
If my admission to UofL Health is a result of a work-related injury, | hereby waive any privilege | may have with
UofL Health, or other healthcare provider, and | hereby authorize these providers to provide the worker's
compensation administrator any information related to my injury or to my past relevant medical history. In the
event there is a dispute about the compensability of my claim or workers compensation benefits, and if my
employer is not specifically determined by a Court of the Department of Labor to be responsible for worker's
compensation medical expenses for the condition or injury that is;the basis of my admission, | agree to be
personally responsible for all such expenses. | further agree that, if my worker's compensation claim is settled
with my employer on a disputed basis without a specific finding that such is compensable as a worker’s
compensation injury, I (or my attorney, if | am represented) -will withhold sufficient funds from any settlement to
pay all amounts owed to UofL Health for treatment of the condition which is the basis for this admission, and |
hereby grant an assignment to UofL Health for payment of all such expenses under such circumstances.
PERSONAL EQUIPMENT AND VALUABLES
| understand that UofL Health does not accept responsibility and will not reimburse me for the loss of money,
jewelry, eyewear, hearing aids, dentures, clothing or other personal property or valuables | bring to UofL. Health.
| take full responsibility for such items and agree to release UofL Health from any and all liability from damage,
loss or theft of such items unless, as applicable, the items are deposited at UofL Health safe for safekeeping. |
also understand that | must inform a nurse if | bring any electrical equipment to UofL Health (e.g., home insulin
pumps; BiPAP machine, CPAP machine) and adhere to UofL Health policies regarding its use. 1assume full
responsibility for such electrical equipment and for any injury caused by the use of the electrical equipment
brought from home.
COMMUNICATIONS
By providing my cell, landline, or any other phone number(s), | expressly consent to receiving communications
from UofL Health, its staff, its contractors, collection agents, and others, at any numbers | provide or that are
later acquired for me. These parties may use this information to contact me by live agent, voice mail, text
message, using an auto dialer or other computer assisted technology, pre-recorded message(s), or by any
other form of electronic communication for any purpose including, but not limited to, appointment and follow-up
health care reminders, scheduling, my account(s), assignment of benefits, and/or financial responsibility. |
understand that depending on my phone plan | could be charged for these calls or text messages. | agree to
provide new number(s) if my number(s) change(s). Providing these numbers is not a condition of receiving
healthcare services.

USING AND SHARING MY INFORMATI
The Law: There is a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996
(“HIPAA”). This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients’ treatment, contact,
and financial information. Taken together, this information is called your “Health Information”. There are also
other federal and/or state laws that require UofL Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of
Health Information, including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health;
developmental disabilities; treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and
counseling; HIV/AIDS; sexual assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic
abuse of an adult with a disability; child abuse and neglect.
Authorization and Notice of Privacy Practices (“NPP”):If my permission is required by law, by signing this
form | agree that UofL Health may receive, use and disclose my Health Information as set forth in this Consent
and as set forth in UofL Health’s NPP. | understand that | can find more information about my rights to my
Health Information, and about how UofL Health uses my Health Information, in the NPP. ] acknowledge that if |
requested a copy of the NPP that | have been given a copy. | further understand that the NPP is available on
UofL Health’s website at:_www.uoflhealth.org.
| agree that my permission applies to all of my Health Information in UofL Health's possession, including but not
limited to my contact information, problem list, diagnostic test results, medication list, allergy list, immunizations,
medical history, surgeries, procedures, and other clinically relevant data.
| understand that UofL Health cannot control how others that receive my Health Information will protect or use
my information. | understand that others may not be required by law to protect my Health Information.
Purposes for which my Health Information may be shared: | understand that UofL. Health may receive, use,
-and disclose my Health Information for the purposes outlined in the NPP. In particular, UofL Health may use
and disclose my Health Information for the following purposes:
Data Sharing Program Purposes: | understand and agree that the use and disclosure of my health
information for certain aspects of treatment at UofL Health may be disclosed to other people involved with my
care outside UofL Health. If | desire to revoke my consent, even in an emergency situation, | must notify UofL
Health’s Health Information Management Department by phone: [PHONE-249], option 2. | understand and
agree that my request will be evaluated to determine if it is reasonable and in the best interest of my health care
to comply with my request. | will be notified in writing of as to whether UofL Health will be able to grant my
request. If my request is granted and I am are in need of emergency treatment, Uofl. Health may end the
restriction if the information is needed to provide my care. (See our Notice of Privacy Practices for more
information on these types of uses and disclosures for further information.)
Fundraising Activities: UofL Health relies on fundraising to help support caring for all patients. | give my
permission to be contacted relating to fundraising opportunities. If ! prefer not to be contacted about fundraising,
! must notify UofL Health by email to: [EMAIL-250] or by phone [PHONE-251]
Operational Purposes: | agree that the contact information I give to UofL Health, such as telephone numbers
and email addresses, may be used by UofL Health and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with
me for operational purposes including appointment reminders, follow up treatment reminders, flu shot
reminders, and patient surveys.

As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be
given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common
side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may
include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and
driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or
questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time,
which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal
symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and
nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Education Materials
Abdominal Pain, Adult
Pain in the abdomen (abdominal pain) can be caused by many things. Often, abdominal pain is not serious and it gets better with no
treatment or by being treated at home. However, sometimes abdominal pain is serious.
Your health care provider will ask questions about your medical history and do a physical exam to try to determine the cause of your
abdominal pain.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider.
• Do not take a laxative unless told by your health care provider.
General instructions
• Watch your condition for any changes.
• Drink enough fluid to keep your urine pale yellow.
• Keep all follow-up visits as told by your health care provider. This is important.
Contact a health care provider if:
• Your abdominal pain changes or gets worse.
• You are not hungry or you lose weight without trying.
• You are constipated or have diarrhea for more than 2–3 days.
• You have pain when you urinate or have a bowel movement.
• Your abdominal pain wakes you up at night.
• Your pain gets worse with meals, after eating, or with certain foods.
• You are vomiting and cannot keep anything down.
• You have a fever.
• You have blood in your urine.
Get help right away if:
• Your pain does not go away as soon as your health care provider told you to expect.
• You cannot stop vomiting.

—46 Cracked lips.
—46 Dry mouth.
—46 Sunken eyes.
—46 Sleepiness.
—46 Weakness.
• You have trouble breathing or chest pain.
Summary
• Often, abdominal pain is not serious and it gets better with no treatment or by being treated at home. However, sometimes
abdominal pain is serious.
• Watch your condition for any changes.
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider.
• Contact a health care provider if your abdominal pain changes or gets worse.
• Get help right away if you have severe pain, cramping, or bloating in your abdomen.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.

Cigarette Smoking
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline: 988
The 988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline is a national network of local crisis centers that provides free and confidential emotional support to
people in suicidal crisis or emotional distress 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. 
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.
• Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
• 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
• Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:
Nausea
Feeling of
"fullness" in
chest
Jaw Pain
Pain that travels
down one or
both arms
Fatigue/being
tired Anxiety Back Pain
Chest pressure,
squeezing, or
discomfort
Shortness of
breath
Sweating, or a
cold sweat
Feeling of
impending
doom
There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
• Fainting/dizziness
• Weakness
• Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.
Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure
Family History Obesity Age

Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.
Why Hands-Only CPR?
• Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
• Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
• 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse
• 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute
Save a life!
4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.
• Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
1
PREVENT
INFECTIONS
• Take good care of
chronic conditions.
• Talk to your doctor
about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
2
PRACTICE GOOD
HYGIENE
• Wash your hands
frequently.
• Keep cuts or open
sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.
3
KNOW THE
SYMPTOMS
• Confusion or
disorientation

Emergency
• Shortness of breath
• High heart rate
• Fever, shivering, or
feeling very cold
• Extreme pain or
discomfort
• Clammy or sweaty
skin
4 ACT FAST
• Get medical care
IMMEDIATELY if
you suspect sepsis
or if you have an
infection that is not
getting better or is
getting worse.
To learn more about sepsis and how to prevent infections, visit www.cdc.gov/sepsis.

The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.

in strict accordance with principles of ALARA.

Abdomen:
The lung bases are clear. The liver is normal. The gallbladder is normal. The
pancreas, spleen, adrenal glands, and kidneys demonstrate no acute pathology.
There is no free air or lymph node enlargement. Abdominal aorta is not aneurysmal.
Pelvis:
There seems to be excessive colon stool. There is a sinus tract from the anus
through the left aspect of the perineum to the lower gluteal cleft. There is no
fluid collection associated. There is no bowel wall thickening or obstruction.
There is no free fluid. Lymph nodes are not enlarged. Urinary bladder is
unremarkable.
Skeleton:
There are no acute fractures. No suspicious bony lesions.
IMPRESSION:
Excessive colon stool, as a subjective observation.
Left perineal anocutaneous sinus tract, appearing unchanged compared with MR
4/21/2023. No fluid collection associated

General Consent on Admission
The term “UofL Health” means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as} well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
| give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the Course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, |consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT and RECOGNITION OF INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS
| have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. | consent to and authorize such care including but
not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services") performed by my
admitting and treating physicians.
| understand and acknowledge that Physicians and certain other practitioners who may treat meor have involvement
in my care are not employees of UofL Health or any of its facilities. | also understand that UofL Health and its
facilities are not responsible for the actions of physicians and other independent contractor practitioners|who treat me
or have involvement in my care at the UofL Health facilities. | further understand these independent contractors
include Physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners, including, but not limited to, nurses employed by
physician groups, certified registered nurse anesthetists (CRNAs), and Physicians’ assistants employed by physician
groups. | understand that the physicians include, but are not limited to, emergency room physicians, radiologists,
anesthesiologists, surgeons, internists, etc. | also understand that there may be medical students, |medical and
surgical residents invarious fields, and/or fellows involved in my care and that these individuals ate not employed or
otherwise agents of the UofL Health or its facilities. | further understand that UofL Heath and its facilities are not
liable for their actions. | understand that at times, the facility may bill for physician services under @contractual
agreement and that UofL Health does not assume liability for the independent contractors’ actions by providing this
service.
| understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are noguarantees concerning the outcome or results
of this treatment and/or examination and | have the right to make decisions concerning my health care, including the
right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
| understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, | may be tested) for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or any
airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic abe |also
understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as an emergency worker,
fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although | will be informed of the right to consent to testing for HIV or
other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be performed on previously gathered
bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing. Information concerning the fact that a
test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and be disclosed by UofL Health only as
permitted by law.
FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY
| agree that | obligate myself and/or the Patient to pay the account(s) of Uofl Health in accordance with the
established rates and payment policy of UofL Health. | also understand that patient/guarantor payments can be
applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or other
sources.
| understand that if my Insurer denies all or any part of UofL Health’s charges for any reason, or |f | have no
insurance, | will be personally and fully responsible for payment of UofL Health’s charges. | am aware that | must
notify the Business Office and submit the completed application form if | believe | may qualify for financial assistance.
\/My Designated Health Care Representative authorizes billing by and direct payment to UofL Health or to the
physicians providing Services at UofL Health. | understand they will bill my insurance directly for their Services, at a
rate not to exceed the UofL Health’s or physician’s regular charges. Insurance includes but is not limited to, my
medical health insurance policy/policies, including my employee health benefit plan, accident, worker’s campensation
benefits, motor vehicle insurance, casualty insurance, and uninsured or underinsured insurance

AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL
| understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and
semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. | hereby agree that the
difference inthe cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if | request one at any
point during mystay.
| hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under any
applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my Authorized
Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that | may have under such insurance
policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to pursue such claim,
right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan, including the right and
ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by the provisions of the
Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").
| also authorize UofL Health to act on my behalf to (1) obtain copies of my insurance policy or benefit plan
documents from my insurer(s) or other Plan Administrator; (2) pursue appeals of adverse benefits decisions, claims
for breaches of fiduciary duty under ERISA, external appeal review under Federal or State statute, administrative
hearings, or legal actions to obtain payment from any payor; (3) disclose my protected health information to my
insurer(s), its affiliates, any plan fiduciary, or independent review organization that may be involved in the resolution
of claims, inconnection with filing or appealing any claim for benefits due; and (4) receive any notices in connection
with my benefit claims or appeals concerning same.
If my admission to UofL Health is a result of a work-related injury, | hereby waive any privilege | may have with UofL
Health, or other healthcare provider, and | hereby authorize these providers to provide the worker's compensation
administrator any information related to my injury or to my past relevant medical history. In the event there is a
dispute about the compensability of my claim or worker's compensation benefits, and if my employer is not
specifically determined by a Court of the Department of Labor to be responsible for worker's compensation medical
expenses for the condition or injury that is the basis of my admission, | agree to bepersonally responsible for all such
expenses. | further agree that, if my worker's compensation claim is settled with my employer on a disputed basis
without a specific finding that such is compensable as a worker's compensation injury, | (or my attorney, if | am
represented) will withhold sufficient funds from any settlement to pay all amounts owed to UofL Health for treatment
of the condition which is the basis for this admission, and |hereby grant an assignment to UofL Health for payment of
all such expenses under such circumstances.
PERSONAL EQUIPMENT AND VALUABLES
| understand that UofL Health does not accept responsibility and will not reimburse mefor the loss of money, jewelry,
eyewear, hearing aids, dentures, clothing or other personal property or valuables | bring to UofL Health. | take full
responsibility for such items and agree to release UofL Health from any and all liability from damage, loss or theft of
such items unless, as applicable, the items are deposited at UofL Health safe for safekeeping. | also understand that
| must inform a nurse if | bring any electrical equipment to UofL Health (e.g., home insulin pumps; BiPAP machine,
CPAP machine) and adhere to UofL Health policies regarding its use. | assume full responsibility for such electrical
equipment and for any injury caused by the use of the electrical equipment brought from home.
COMMUNICATIONS
By providing my cell, landline, or any other phone number(s), | expressly consent to receiving communications from
UofL Health, its staff, its contractors, collection agents, and others, at any numbers | provide or that are later
acquired for me. These parties may use this information to contact me by live agent, voice mail, text message, using
an auto dialer or other computer assisted technology, pre-recorded message(s), or by any other form of electronic
communication for any purpose including, but not limited to, appointment and follow-up health care reminders,
scheduling, my account(s), assignment of benefits, and/or financial responsibility. | understand that depending on my
phone plan | could be charged for these calls or text messages. | agree to provide new number(s) if my number(s)
change(s). Providing these numbers is not a condition of receiving healthcare services.

USING AND SHARING MY INFORM
The Law: There is a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability oat —— Act of 1996 (“HIPAA”).
This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients’ treatment, cof financial
information. Taken together, this information is called your “Health Information”. There are also other federal and/or
state laws that require Uofl Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of Health Information,
including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health; developmental disabilities;
treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and counseling; HIV/AIDS; sexual
assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic abuse of an adult wa a disability;
child abuse and neglect.
Authorization and Notice of Privacy Practices (“NPP”):If my permission is required by law, by signing this form |
agree that UofL Health may receive, use and disclose my Health Information as set forth in this Consent and as set
forth in UofL Health’s NPP. | understand that | can find more information about my rights to my Health Information,
and about how UofL Health uses my Health Information, inthe NPP. | acknowledge that if | requestedja copy of the
NPP that | have been given a copy. | further understand that the NPP is available on UofL Health’ website at:
www.uoflhealth.org.
| agree that my permission applies to all of my Health Information in UofL Health’s possession, including but not
limited to my contact information, problem list, diagnostic test results, medication list, allergy list, immunizations,
medical history, surgeries, procedures, and other clinically relevant data.
| understand that UofL Health cannot control how others that receive my Health Information will prot t or use my
information. | understand that others may not be required by law to protect my Health Information.
Purposes for which my Health Information may be shared: | understand that UofL Health may receive, use, and
disclose my Health Information for the purposes outlined in the NPP. In particular, UofL Health may use/and disclose
my Health Information for the following purposes:
Data Sharing Program Purposes: | understand and agree that the use and disclosure of my health information for
certain aspects of treatment at UofL Health may be disclosed to other people involved with my care butside UofL
Health. If | desire to revoke my consent, even in an emergency situation, | must notify UoflL Health’s Health
Information Management Department by phone: [PHONE-403], option 2. | understand and agree that my request
will be evaluated to determine if itis reasonable and in the best interest of my health care to comply with my request.
|will be notified in writing of as to whether UofL Health will be able to grant my request. If my request is granted and |
am are in need of emergency treatment, UofL Health may end the restriction if the information is needed to provide
my care. (See our Notice of Privacy Practices for more information on these types of uses and disclosures for
further information.)
Fundraising Activities: UofL Health relies on fundraising to help support caring for all patients. | give my permission
to be contacted relating to fundraising opportunities. If | prefer not to be contacted about fundraising, | must notify
UofL Health by email to: elea.fox @uoflhealth.org or by phone [PHONE-404]
Operational Purposes: | agree that the contact information | give to UofL Health, such as telephone numbers and
email addresses, may be used by UofL Health and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with me for
operational purposes including appointment reminders, follow up treatment reminders, flu shot reminders, and
patient surveys.

TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
| understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, | may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-—19 or
any airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic
purposes. | also understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as
an emergency worker, fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although | will be informed of the right to
consent to testing for HIV or other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be
performed on previously gathered bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing.
Information concerning the fact that a test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and
be disclosed by UofL Health only as permitted by law.

applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or
other sources.
